House File 200 - Introduced


                                 HOUSE FILE 

                                 HOUSE FILE 
                                 HOUSE FILE                                  HOUSE FILE                                  BY  MASCHER

 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act relating to the maintenance and administration of
  2    epinephrine in schools and certain other facilities.
  3 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:
    TLSB 2138HH (2) 86
    je/nh

    je/nh

PAG LIN



  1  1    Section 1.      je/nh

PAG LIN



  1  1    Section 1.  

  1  1    Section 1.  
  1  1    Section 1.    1  1    Section 1.    1  2 supply.
  1  3    1.  For purposes of this section, unless the context
  1  4 otherwise requires:
  1  5    a.  "Epinephrine auto=injector" means the same as provided
  1  6 in section 280.16.
  1  7    b.  "Facility" means a food establishment as defined in
  1  8 section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in section 88A.1, a
  1  9 recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a sports area.
  1 10    c.  "Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" means
  1 11 an employee of a facility who is trained and authorized to
  1 12 administer an epinephrine auto=injector.
  1 13    d.  "Physician" means the same as provided in section 280.16.
  1 14    2.  Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the
  1 15 contrary, a physician may prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors
  1 16 in the name of a facility to be maintained for use as provided
  1 17 in this section.
  1 18    3.  A facility may obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  1 19 auto=injectors and maintain a supply of such auto=injectors in
  1 20 a secure location at each location where a member of the public
  1 21 may be present for use as provided in this section. A facility
  1 22 that obtains such a prescription shall replace epinephrine
  1 23 auto=injectors in the supply upon use or expiration. Personnel
  1 24 authorized to administer epinephrine may possess and administer
  1 25 epinephrine auto=injectors from the supply as provided in this
  1 26 section.
  1 27    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  1 28 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  1 29 facility's supply to an individual present at the facility
  1 30 if such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the
  1 31 individual is having an anaphylactic reaction.
  1 32    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  1 33 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration of
  1 34 an epinephrine auto=injector to an individual present at the
  1 35 facility who such personnel reasonably and in good faith
  2  1 believe to be having an anaphylactic reaction; a facility
  2  2 employing the personnel; the owner or operator of the facility;
  2  3 or the prescriber of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall
  2  4 incur no liability, except for gross negligence, as a result
  2  5 of any injury arising from the provision, administration,
  2  6 or assistance in the administration of an epinephrine
  2  7 auto=injector as provided in this section.
  2  8    6.  The department of public health, the board of medicine,
  2  9 and the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  2 10 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  2 11 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  2 12 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  2 13 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  2 14 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  2 15 epinephrine.
  2 16    Sec. 2.  Section 280.16, Code 2015, is amended to read as
  2 17 follows:

  1 28 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  1 29 facility's supply to an individual present at the facility
  1 30 if such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the
  1 31 individual is having an anaphylactic reaction.
  1 32    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  1 33 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration of
  1 34 an epinephrine auto=injector to an individual present at the
  1 35 facility who such personnel reasonably and in good faith
  2  1 believe to be having an anaphylactic reaction; a facility
  2  2 employing the personnel; the owner or operator of the facility;
  2  3 or the prescriber of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall
  2  4 incur no liability, except for gross negligence, as a result
  2  5 of any injury arising from the provision, administration,
  2  6 or assistance in the administration of an epinephrine
  2  7 auto=injector as provided in this section.
  2  8    6.  The department of public health, the board of medicine,
  2  9 and the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  2 10 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  2 11 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  2 12 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  2 13 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  2 14 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  2 15 epinephrine.

  5  1    1.  For purposes of this section, unless the context
  5  2 otherwise requires:
  5  3    a.  "Epinephrine auto=injector" means the same as provided
  5  4 in section 280.16.
  5  5    b.  "Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine"
  5  6 means a school nurse or other employee of a school district
  5  7 or accredited nonpublic school trained and authorized to
  5  8 administer an epinephrine auto=injector.
  5  9    c.  "Physician" means the same as provided in section 280.16.
  5 10    2.  Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the
  5 11 contrary, a physician may prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 12 in the name of a school district or accredited nonpublic school
  5 13 to be maintained for use as provided in this section.
  5 14    3.  The board of directors in charge of each school district
  5 15 and the authorities in charge of each accredited nonpublic
  5 16 school may obtain a prescription for epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 17 and maintain a supply of such auto=injectors in a secure
  5 18 location at each school for use as provided in this section.
  5 19 The board and the authorities shall replace epinephrine
  5 20 auto=injectors in the supply upon use or expiration. Personnel
  5 21 authorized to administer epinephrine may possess and administer
  5 22 epinephrine auto=injectors from the supply as provided in this
  5 23 section.
  5 24    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  5 25 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  5 26 school's supply to a student if such personnel reasonably and
  5 27 in good faith believe the student is having an anaphylactic
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.
  6 15                           EXPLANATION
  6 16 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  6 18    This bill permits the board of directors in charge of
  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician
  6 30 to prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors in the name of a school
  6 31 district or accredited nonpublic school to be maintained
  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.
  6 34    The bill permits personnel authorized to administer
  6 35 epinephrine to provide or administer an epinephrine
  7  1 auto=injector from a school's supply to a student if such
  7  2 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the student is
  7  3 having an anaphylactic reaction.
  7  4    The bill provides immunity from legal liability, except for
  7  5 gross negligence, to any personnel authorized to administer
  7  6 epinephrine who provide, administer, or assist in the
  7  7 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student
  7  8 who such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to
  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86

  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5  3    a.  "Epinephrine auto=injector" means the same as provided
  5  4 in section 280.16.
  5  5    b.  "Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine"
  5  6 means a school nurse or other employee of a school district
  5  7 or accredited nonpublic school trained and authorized to
  5  8 administer an epinephrine auto=injector.
  5  9    c.  "Physician" means the same as provided in section 280.16.
  5 10    2.  Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the
  5 11 contrary, a physician may prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 12 in the name of a school district or accredited nonpublic school
  5 13 to be maintained for use as provided in this section.
  5 14    3.  The board of directors in charge of each school district
  5 15 and the authorities in charge of each accredited nonpublic
  5 16 school may obtain a prescription for epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 17 and maintain a supply of such auto=injectors in a secure
  5 18 location at each school for use as provided in this section.
  5 19 The board and the authorities shall replace epinephrine
  5 20 auto=injectors in the supply upon use or expiration. Personnel
  5 21 authorized to administer epinephrine may possess and administer
  5 22 epinephrine auto=injectors from the supply as provided in this
  5 23 section.
  5 24    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  5 25 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  5 26 school's supply to a student if such personnel reasonably and
  5 27 in good faith believe the student is having an anaphylactic
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.
  6 15                           EXPLANATION
  6 16 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  6 18    This bill permits the board of directors in charge of
  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician
  6 30 to prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors in the name of a school
  6 31 district or accredited nonpublic school to be maintained
  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.
  6 34    The bill permits personnel authorized to administer
  6 35 epinephrine to provide or administer an epinephrine
  7  1 auto=injector from a school's supply to a student if such
  7  2 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the student is
  7  3 having an anaphylactic reaction.
  7  4    The bill provides immunity from legal liability, except for
  7  5 gross negligence, to any personnel authorized to administer
  7  6 epinephrine who provide, administer, or assist in the
  7  7 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student
  7  8 who such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to
  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.

  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration

  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5  7 or accredited nonpublic school trained and authorized to
  5  8 administer an epinephrine auto=injector.
  5  9    c.  "Physician" means the same as provided in section 280.16.
  5 10    2.  Notwithstanding any other provision of law to the
  5 11 contrary, a physician may prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 12 in the name of a school district or accredited nonpublic school
  5 13 to be maintained for use as provided in this section.
  5 14    3.  The board of directors in charge of each school district
  5 15 and the authorities in charge of each accredited nonpublic
  5 16 school may obtain a prescription for epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 17 and maintain a supply of such auto=injectors in a secure
  5 18 location at each school for use as provided in this section.
  5 19 The board and the authorities shall replace epinephrine
  5 20 auto=injectors in the supply upon use or expiration. Personnel
  5 21 authorized to administer epinephrine may possess and administer
  5 22 epinephrine auto=injectors from the supply as provided in this
  5 23 section.
  5 24    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  5 25 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  5 26 school's supply to a student if such personnel reasonably and
  5 27 in good faith believe the student is having an anaphylactic
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.

  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board

  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5 11 contrary, a physician may prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 12 in the name of a school district or accredited nonpublic school
  5 13 to be maintained for use as provided in this section.
  5 14    3.  The board of directors in charge of each school district
  5 15 and the authorities in charge of each accredited nonpublic
  5 16 school may obtain a prescription for epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 17 and maintain a supply of such auto=injectors in a secure
  5 18 location at each school for use as provided in this section.
  5 19 The board and the authorities shall replace epinephrine
  5 20 auto=injectors in the supply upon use or expiration. Personnel
  5 21 authorized to administer epinephrine may possess and administer
  5 22 epinephrine auto=injectors from the supply as provided in this
  5 23 section.
  5 24    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  5 25 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  5 26 school's supply to a student if such personnel reasonably and
  5 27 in good faith believe the student is having an anaphylactic
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.
  6 15                           EXPLANATION
  6 16 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  6 18    This bill permits the board of directors in charge of
  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician

  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.

  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.

  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5 15 and the authorities in charge of each accredited nonpublic
  5 16 school may obtain a prescription for epinephrine auto=injectors
  5 17 and maintain a supply of such auto=injectors in a secure
  5 18 location at each school for use as provided in this section.
  5 19 The board and the authorities shall replace epinephrine
  5 20 auto=injectors in the supply upon use or expiration. Personnel
  5 21 authorized to administer epinephrine may possess and administer
  5 22 epinephrine auto=injectors from the supply as provided in this
  5 23 section.
  5 24    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  5 25 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  5 26 school's supply to a student if such personnel reasonably and
  5 27 in good faith believe the student is having an anaphylactic
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.
  6 15                           EXPLANATION
  6 16 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  6 18    This bill permits the board of directors in charge of
  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician
  6 30 to prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors in the name of a school
  6 31 district or accredited nonpublic school to be maintained
  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.
  6 34    The bill permits personnel authorized to administer
  6 35 epinephrine to provide or administer an epinephrine
  7  1 auto=injector from a school's supply to a student if such
  7  2 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the student is
  7  3 having an anaphylactic reaction.
  7  4    The bill provides immunity from legal liability, except for
  7  5 gross negligence, to any personnel authorized to administer
  7  6 epinephrine who provide, administer, or assist in the
  7  7 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student
  7  8 who such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to
  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.

  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5 19 The board and the authorities shall replace epinephrine
  5 20 auto=injectors in the supply upon use or expiration. Personnel
  5 21 authorized to administer epinephrine may possess and administer
  5 22 epinephrine auto=injectors from the supply as provided in this
  5 23 section.
  5 24    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  5 25 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  5 26 school's supply to a student if such personnel reasonably and
  5 27 in good faith believe the student is having an anaphylactic
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.
  6 15                           EXPLANATION
  6 16 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  6 18    This bill permits the board of directors in charge of
  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician
  6 30 to prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors in the name of a school
  6 31 district or accredited nonpublic school to be maintained
  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.
  6 34    The bill permits personnel authorized to administer
  6 35 epinephrine to provide or administer an epinephrine
  7  1 auto=injector from a school's supply to a student if such
  7  2 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the student is
  7  3 having an anaphylactic reaction.
  7  4    The bill provides immunity from legal liability, except for
  7  5 gross negligence, to any personnel authorized to administer
  7  6 epinephrine who provide, administer, or assist in the
  7  7 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student
  7  8 who such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to
  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86

  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician
  6 30 to prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors in the name of a school
  6 31 district or accredited nonpublic school to be maintained
  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.
  6 34    The bill permits personnel authorized to administer
  6 35 epinephrine to provide or administer an epinephrine
  7  1 auto=injector from a school's supply to a student if such
  7  2 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the student is
  7  3 having an anaphylactic reaction.
  7  4    The bill provides immunity from legal liability, except for
  7  5 gross negligence, to any personnel authorized to administer
  7  6 epinephrine who provide, administer, or assist in the
  7  7 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student
  7  8 who such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to
  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5 24    4.  Personnel authorized to administer epinephrine may
  5 25 provide or administer an epinephrine auto=injector from the
  5 26 school's supply to a student if such personnel reasonably and
  5 27 in good faith believe the student is having an anaphylactic
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.

  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.

  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board

  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board

  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5 28 reaction.
  5 29    5.  Any personnel authorized to administer epinephrine
  5 30 who provide, administer, or assist in the administration
  5 31 of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student who such
  5 32 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to be having
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.
  6 15                           EXPLANATION
  6 16 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  6 18    This bill permits the board of directors in charge of
  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician
  6 30 to prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors in the name of a school
  6 31 district or accredited nonpublic school to be maintained
  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.
  6 34    The bill permits personnel authorized to administer
  6 35 epinephrine to provide or administer an epinephrine
  7  1 auto=injector from a school's supply to a student if such
  7  2 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the student is
  7  3 having an anaphylactic reaction.
  7  4    The bill provides immunity from legal liability, except for
  7  5 gross negligence, to any personnel authorized to administer
  7  6 epinephrine who provide, administer, or assist in the
  7  7 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student
  7  8 who such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to
  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86

  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
       LSB 2138HH (2) 86
       je/nh
  5 33 an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or accredited
  5 34 nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board of
  5 35 directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  6  1 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber
  6  2 of the epinephrine auto=injector, shall incur no liability,
  6  3 except for gross negligence, as a result of any injury arising
  6  4 from the provision, administration, or assistance in the
  6  5 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in
  6  6 this section.
  6  7    6.  The department of education, the board of medicine, and
  6  8 the board of pharmacy shall adopt rules pursuant to chapter
  6  9 17A to implement and administer this section, including but
  6 10 not limited to standards and procedures for the prescription,
  6 11 distribution, storage, replacement, and administration of
  6 12 epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training and authorization
  6 13 to be required for personnel authorized to administer
  6 14 epinephrine.
  6 15                           EXPLANATION
  6 16 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  6 17 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  6 18    This bill permits the board of directors in charge of
  6 19 each school district and the authorities in charge of an
  6 20 accredited nonpublic school to maintain in a secure location
  6 21 at each school a supply of epinephrine auto=injectors for
  6 22 use as provided in the bill. The bill requires the board
  6 23 and authorities to replace epinephrine auto=injectors in the
  6 24 supply upon use or expiration. The bill permits the board
  6 25 and authorities to obtain a prescription for epinephrine
  6 26 auto=injectors for use as provided in the bill. The bill
  6 27 permits personnel authorized to administer epinephrine to
  6 28 possess and administer epinephrine auto=injectors from the
  6 29 supply as provided in the bill. The bill permits a physician
  6 30 to prescribe epinephrine auto=injectors in the name of a school
  6 31 district or accredited nonpublic school to be maintained
  6 32 for use as provided in the bill, notwithstanding any other
  6 33 provision of law to the contrary.
  6 34    The bill permits personnel authorized to administer
  6 35 epinephrine to provide or administer an epinephrine
  7  1 auto=injector from a school's supply to a student if such
  7  2 personnel reasonably and in good faith believe the student is
  7  3 having an anaphylactic reaction.
  7  4    The bill provides immunity from legal liability, except for
  7  5 gross negligence, to any personnel authorized to administer
  7  6 epinephrine who provide, administer, or assist in the
  7  7 administration of an epinephrine auto=injector to a student
  7  8 who such personnel reasonably and in good faith believe to
  7  9 be having an anaphylactic reaction; a school district or
  7 10 accredited nonpublic school employing the personnel; the board
  7 11 of directors in charge of the school district or authorities in
  7 12 charge of the accredited nonpublic school; or the prescriber of
  7 13 the epinephrine auto=injector,  for any injury arising from the
  7 14 provision, administration, or assistance in the administration
  7 15 of an epinephrine auto=injector as provided in the bill.
  7 16    The bill defines "epinephrine auto=injector" as a medical
  7 17 device for immediate self=administration of a measured dose
  7 18 of epinephrine by a person at risk of anaphylaxis. The bill
  7 19 defines "personnel authorized to administer epinephrine" as
  7 20 an employee who is trained and authorized to administer an
  7 21 epinephrine auto=injector.
  7 22    The bill permits certain facilities to maintain a supply of
  7 23 epinephrine auto=injectors in the same fashion at locations
  7 24 where members of the public may be present, with the same
  7 25 duties, powers, and immunities relating to maintaining a
  7 26 supply of epinephrine auto=injectors and administering the
  7 27 auto=injectors applying if the facility chooses to do so.  The
  7 28 bill defines "facility" as a food establishment as defined in
  7 29 Code section 137F.1, a carnival as defined in Code section
  7 30 88A.1, a recreational camp, a youth sports facility, or a
  7 31 sports area.
  7 32    The bill requires the department of education, the
  7 33 department of public health, the board of medicine, and the
  7 34 board of pharmacy to adopt rules to implement and administer
  7 35 the bill, including but not limited to standards and procedures
  8  1 for the prescription, distribution, storage, replacement, and
  8  2 administration of epinephrine auto=injectors, and for training
  8  3 and authorization to be required for personnel authorized to
  8  4 administer epinephrine auto=injectors.
  8  5    The bill also adds epinephrine auto=injectors to Code
  8  6 section 280.16, which permits self=administration of medication
  8  7 in public and nonpublic schools by students with asthma.
  8  8    The bill requires school districts and nonpublic schools
  8  9 to  allow the use of an epinephrine auto=injector by a student
  8 10 with a written statement from a physician on file if the school
  8 11 receives written authorization and certain medical information
  8 12 from the student's parent or guardian.
  8 13    The bill permits a student with a written statement
  8 14 from a physician on file to possess and use an epinephrine
  8 15 auto=injector while in school, at school=sponsored activities,
  8 16 under the supervision of school personnel, and before or after
  8 17 normal school activities, such as while in before=school or
  8 18 after=school care on school=operated property. The bill
  8 19 requires a school district or nonpublic school to notify a
  8 20 student's parent or guardian before withdrawing the privilege
  8 21 to use an epinephrine auto=injector.
  8 22    The bill adds epinephrine auto=injectors to the provisions
  8 23 of Code section 280.16 granting immunity from legal liability
  8 24 to school employees, except for gross negligence, for injuries
  8 25 resulting from the self=administration of medication. Code
  8 26 section 280.16 requires a student's parent or guardian to
  8 27 receive notice of such immunity.
